<div id="review_57998624" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/57998624" />
    <a title="Donalyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/829035-donalyn"><img alt="Donalyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577941818p2/829035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/57998624?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donalyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donalyn" href="/user/show/829035-donalyn">Donalyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/829035-donalyn?shelf=ya-science-fiction">ya-science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer57998624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer435910155502554805">Gabry, Mary's daughter, fears life and love. She seems to blame herself for everything that happens, including the poor choices of the other characters. I have not read so much whining and self-loathing since Bella Swan. <br/><br/>This companion to The Forest of Hands and Teeth didn't advance the story of life after the Return and left little hope for the characters' futures.<br/><br/>Still, Carrie Ryan's writing is beautiful with moments of tenderness, longing, and tragedy. </span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_102007201" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102007201" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/862743-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1284696487p2/862743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102007201?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/862743-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer102007201&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102007201" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2697093375167957181">Pretty much a letdown. I really enjoyed the companion novel, "The Forest of Hands and Teeth," and I figured that this story would add to the world created in that book. Unfortunately, it didn't; and I even feel like the original story's effect is diminished because of this books incessant attempt at playing it safe. Not only did this book not add to the post-Return mythos, it didn't add anything to the pre-Return storyline either. There is a lot of mystery left to explore at the end of the first</span>
  <span id="freeText2697093375167957181" style="display:none">Pretty much a letdown. I really enjoyed the companion novel, "The Forest of Hands and Teeth," and I figured that this story would add to the world created in that book. Unfortunately, it didn't; and I even feel like the original story's effect is diminished because of this books incessant attempt at playing it safe. Not only did this book not add to the post-Return mythos, it didn't add anything to the pre-Return storyline either. There is a lot of mystery left to explore at the end of the first book regarding the causes of the Return, and this book does nothing to shed any light on those tantalizing details that are missing.<br /><br />Instead, we are thrust into the same exact world as before, forced to follow a nearly identical plot structure to "The Forest of Hands and Teeth," minus the tension of the unknown. Now that we know that other factions exist in this world (and in fact, there are large cities with an overarching governing body), the tension of the novel is erased. We know that there are survivors. We know that these characters aren't stranded, alone, in a post-apocalyptic wasteland. Now, armed with the knowledge that there are militaries and cities and thousands of people still alive, our characters look like pathetic, idiotic people who can't get organized enough to kill off the shambling masses of Unconsecrated. I guess, in the future, a coordinated effort to exterminate the Unconsecrated is too far-fetched. Or maybe it's just a technicality that Ryan chose to leave out of her narrative because explaining it away would have been too inconvenient. <br /><br />Our protagonist is Gabry, the daughter of Mary (the main character of the original novel). Mary, in a plot device that completely undermines her entire dramatic character arc from the first novel, leaves Gabry to go back where she feels she belongs: the forest. Gabry, meanwhile, decides to go into the forest because she ventured beyond the city gates one night with friends, got caught, and now her friends are being forced into army servitude. The forest, in her mind, is her friends only escape from army recruitment.<br /><br />What follows is nearly identical to the first story, just told in reverse. Yes, there is another love triangle. Yes, Unconsecrated show up and people die. Yes, they make it back to the Mary's original hometown from the original book. But what's the point? The book really doesn't seem like it has much to say; which is a shame, because "The Forest of Hands and Teeth" truly felt like it did. It's not even really that interesting. Beyond some semi-exciting zombie attack scenes, there is really nothing to differentiate this book from the original. This is, in my opinion, a pale imitation of Ryan's first book. It is, ultimately, inconsequential and unnecessary.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2697093375167957181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2023299482" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2023299482" />
    <a title="Farren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29738019-farren"><img alt="Farren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438296630p2/29738019.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2023299482?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Farren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Farren" href="/user/show/29738019-farren">Farren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29738019-farren?shelf=ya-sci-fi-dystopia">ya-sci-fi-dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29738019-farren?shelf=ya-horror">ya-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29738019-farren?shelf=library-audiobook">library-audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2023299482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2266876478673966105"><b>1.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I hated this book. It was just plain awful. I hardly enjoyed the first one, but all the reviews I read said the sequel was way better. It is. If you enjoy reading the same plot structure, another lame love triangle, and a main character who is even more whiny and selfish than the first one, that is.<br/><br/>The beginning was promising, and I even posted in my status update how much more I was liking it than the first book. They sneak into an abandoned amusement park, which was a stupid plan that</span>
  <span id="freeText2266876478673966105" style="display:none"><b>1.5 stars</b><br><br>I hated this book. It was just plain awful. I hardly enjoyed the first one, but all the reviews I read said the sequel was way better. It is. If you enjoy reading the same plot structure, another lame love triangle, and a main character who is even more whiny and selfish than the first one, that is.<br><br>The beginning was promising, and I even posted in my status update how much more I was liking it than the first book. They sneak into an abandoned amusement park, which was a stupid plan that made no sense, but of course I was thinking <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1508207084ra/24190505.gif" width="400" height="246" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and since that's one of the best video games ever I got prematurely excited. I feel so duped.<br><br><b>Here's the good: </b><br><br>Right in the beginning we learn what exactly causes a person to return as a "breaker" zombie. In The Forest of Hands and Teeth they were just like <i>man that is one fast zombie in the strange red vest, and would you just look at that shade of red?! I'm shook!</i><br><br>Okay that's it for the good. <b>So here's the bad:<br><br>Everything.</b><br><br>J/k. Well not really, so I'll be a little more specific.<br><br>*SPOILERS AHEAD BUT WHO CARES BECAUSE THIS BOOK IS JUST LIKE THE FIRST ONE ANYWAY*<br><br>Gabry. Omg this girl could not be any worse. Possibly the worst main character I've ever read, as a matter of fact. When the book begins she is nothing but a scared little girl, never wanting to venture outside of their safe community, which some (me) may think is okay because that's the smart thing to do. But she does it anyway because her best friend and a cute boy told her to, which means that she isn't smart, just afraid and dumb. When she sees a breaker heading towards her loud ass friends she decides not to warn them, lest she draw attention her way instead. After the attack that she didn't prevent, she runs home, crawls into bed, and pretends she was never there to begin with (leaving her crush behind with a zombie bite) because she doesn't want to get in trouble. <br>She basically proceeds to whine and wallow in endless guilt over absolutely everything for the rest of the book. Except for the one thing she should feel terribly guilty over, some may say <b>the worst sin one can commit</b>, but hey, what do I know? She's incredibly selfish and lashes out every time she hears something that she doesn't want to hear, and even physically assaults Elias multiple times in the book. She mentions the marks she leaves on him frequently, but I guess he doesn't mind and it's okay, because he is also wracked with guilt that will not subside and must "deserve" it. Gabry does all these reckless things and puts herself and others in danger, stomps off like a child whenever she's angry, and constantly contradicts herself. I'd like to throw her in the fire from the first book.<br><br>As annoying as Gabry was, Cira was equally as bad. She berates Gabry for playing it safe and convinces her to live a little and go play around in Funland. After the shit hits the fan, she then berates Gabry for lying about her part in it, and tells her that since she didn't get caught it's her responsibility to go back and find her cutie patootie brother. Because going out there as a large group worked out so well for them right? It's totally okay to send your best friend back ALONE this time to look for your probably already dead brother. Rather than being forced into service with the Recruiters (you know, the people with the weapons who have the best chance of survival out of everyone) she decides live just isn't worth living anymore. She wallows in despair as much as Gabry wallows in guilt, which makes them the most intolerable female duo in literature, as well as making all women look weak and irrational.<br><br>The guys are not important enough on their own to discuss, so I'll just talk about the horrid love triangle. <br><blockquote>Omg I love Catcher so much, and he just kissed me so now he's my boyfriend and we're in loooooove.<br>Ooh this guy Elias is so cute and helpful. I'll keep him on the back burner until bf #1 dies.<br>Wow Catcher, you're not dead. Guess we can be together after all.<br>I love how cute and smart Elias looks while he explains everything to me repeatedly because I'm so stupid *sigh*<br>Catcher, let's resume the kissing. No? Good thing I have another boyfriend then!<br>Elias, let's be together forever and ever. Oh no, your leg!<br>I can't make it without you, Catcher, don't leave me. Who else will help me get back to Elias?!</blockquote><br>Somehow still not as annoying as Mary's love triangle though. Also, does Carrie Ryan know that legs aren't the only body parts that can be injured?<br><br>Now I need to mention the immunity. Immunity is so rare that the Recruiters won't tell anyone about it, because they don't want them to get hopeful and keep their loved ones around if they become infected. That part I get. What I don't get is why the villagers don't kill people before they turn to remove the risk of them biting people once they're zombies. If no one believes there is a chance they'll live through it then it's the only logical option. When you watch The Walking Dead they don't wait until they all come back as zombies to kill them because it's too stupid to take that risk for nothing! Why would Gabry want to keep returning to someone who is infected so that she can take care of it after instead of before? And with no weapons at that! She keeps saying over and over again how she was taught there is <i>absolutely no chance</i> of surviving a bite. While I'm on the subject, why the eff is no one armed in this series except for the Recruiters??? What do they plan to do in case of a breach? Why do they rely on one woman to kill the zombies that wash up on the beach all by herself? It's like they want to die or something! Don't even get me started on this zombie worshiping cult either. It made no sense to me.<br><br>Mary was just as self-involved as ever. In the first book she risked everyone's lives just to get the ocean like an absolute moron. In this book she tells Gabry that she isn't her real mother and that she is leaving the ocean to go find the people she left behind some three decades ago. WTF Mary. The only way I'd read the last book is if she dies a horrible, gruesome death.<br><br>I listened to this on audio, and the narration was loads better than the first book. Despite the fact that the narrator pronounced "forest" as "farest" and it bugged the hell out of me.... <br><br>I have <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23281652.Daughter_of_Deep_Silence" title="Daughter of Deep Silence by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">Daughter of Deep Silence</a> but I don't think I can force myself to read Carrie Ryan's work again. I'm beyond done with the poor writing, never-ending, self-pitying internal dialogue, major plot holes, and characters that possess zero good qualities. If the characters are even half as bad in her other novels I know I'd DNF them anyway. I'm still flabbergasted that The Forest of Hands and Teeth got a movie deal. I am confident that it will bomb, so this train wreck will never make it to screen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2266876478673966105" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3027349886" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3027349886" />
    <a title="Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67389898-vee-bookish-ya-book-blogger"><img alt="Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603583342p2/67389898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3027349886?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger" href="/user/show/67389898-vee-bookish-ya-book-blogger">Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575090897" href="/book/show/7804115-the-dead-tossed-waves">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3027349886" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18113113870087258082">It's the sequel to The Forest Of Hands And Teeth! Now with even more angst! Sigh. I was expecting this to be a continuation of Mary's story, so you can imagine my surprise when I read the blurb and saw the name "Gabry". My first guess was the Gabrielle we met in the first book but then I realised that this sequel is set a good 30 years after we met Mary, focusing instead on her daughter.<br/><br/>This should be quite an interesting book - it's set from the perspective of an outsider to The Forest, a girl </span>
  <span id="freeText18113113870087258082" style="display:none">It's the sequel to The Forest Of Hands And Teeth! Now with even more angst! Sigh. I was expecting this to be a continuation of Mary's story, so you can imagine my surprise when I read the blurb and saw the name "Gabry". My first guess was the Gabrielle we met in the first book but then I realised that this sequel is set a good 30 years after we met Mary, focusing instead on her daughter.<br /><br />This should be quite an interesting book - it's set from the perspective of an outsider to The Forest, a girl who grew up in a village protected by the Protectorate, some sort of military types. Gabry lives in a lighthouse and every morning we go zombie bashing because they wash ashore. Bizarre but fun right? Somehow, no. This book dragged so, so much.<br /><br />I may have sneaked a glance at the blurb for book three, so when something major went down at the funfair with Catcher, it was easy to guess where they were going with this. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I actually hate the munie trope but if the book had chosen him as the protagonist it would have been a much better story. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Gabry runs away after the zombie attack at the fairground, leaving everyone to it and when they are caught and Catcher is missing, she goes to look for him. Of course, one missing boyfriend isn't quite enough angst, so cue Elias!<br /><br />Elias is fecking annoying. Okay, so he does save her quite a few times but he sure as hell seems to fall in love with her quickly, despite it being plainly obvious that Catcher is her boyfriend or near as. And then when she doesn't reciprocate he gets irritated with her? What? Is this the behavior we really want to be displaying as normal in teen books? Of course he has a Tragic Backstory, all tied up with the Forest and Gabry because we need EVEN MORE ANGST.<br /><br />One thing that could have saved this book but kind of fell apart was Catcher's sister, Gabry's best friend. With her sentence after the events at the fairground and believing her brother to be dead, it pushes her into depression to the point where she didn't want to live any more. However it devolved into a kinda sometimes she wanted to live sometimes she didn't situation and it didn't have the impact that it should have done.<br /><br />This one does a little better at a plot twist but I didn't have that 'Woah' moment. It was just like... oh okay so that's a thing. I know our next character is Annah in the Dark City, a place that was frequently mentioned in this book. After going from village to other village, I'm really hoping the Dark City is just that - a city. It may just be interesting enough to make the series a complete disappointment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18113113870087258082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer7646721065590915824">I was surprised to find that this book didn't take off where the first one left off. Instead, we're treated to a larger world than just the Forest of Hands and Teeth, one where humanity is surviving a little less desperately than Mary's villages. In this book, we get to know Mary's daughter Gabry, who has grown up in the relative safety of an ocean village, the Unconsecrated a danger they are warned about but never seem to encounter.   <span id="freeText7646721065590915824" style="display:none">I was surprised to find that this book didn't take off where the first one left off. Instead, we're treated to a larger world than just the Forest of Hands and Teeth, one where humanity is surviving a little less desperately than Mary's villages. In this book, we get to know Mary's daughter Gabry, who has grown up in the relative safety of an ocean village, the Unconsecrated a danger they are warned about but never seem to encounter. Until the night the book starts, of course.<br /><br />This book was an awesome adventure, but it felt a lot more formulaic because a lot of the basics were the same. It's got the same kind of love triangle, the adventure is forced down the same path (literally) and the end is similar in another way which I won't specify for now. Though this end seems to have a setup for the book that has to continue in the third, rather than to skip to a new generation.<br /><br />The skipping didn't bother me much. I don't think that Mary was a very relatable character to a lot of people while Gabry seems a lot better. She, at least, wants nothing more than for things to go back to the way they used to be, and she has none of the adventurous spirit that led her mother out of the forest those years ago. Nevertheless, she's pushed by her relationships with her friends and won't give them up, despite continually doubting herself.<br /><br />To go more into the similar ending: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Why does the girl character always have to decide who it is she wants, just to have him snatched away from her at the last minute? In this last book, seconds after Gabry decides she wants Elias, he falls off a cliff. Dramatic, absolutely, but a lot less believable now that it's happened twice in the same series. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Still, the story is interesting and this second book is a great companion to the first and expands the surviving world to show us how others live outside the Forest of Hands and Teeth.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9578345710496346040">Oh, Carrie Ryan, you break my heart. At times while reading it, I wanted to give it 5 stars. At others, I wanted to throw it across the room and give it 1 star. Well, I never give 1 star, but you get the idea. But damn, she writes a good book. I just have to remind myself that "5 stars" doesn't necessarily have to equal "happy". I also have to remind myself that just because a character occassionally might act like a bitch, a crybaby, a scaredy cat, or an idiot, it doesn't mean she's not a good </span>
  <span id="freeText9578345710496346040" style="display:none">Oh, Carrie Ryan, you break my heart. At times while reading it, I wanted to give it 5 stars. At others, I wanted to throw it across the room and give it 1 star. Well, I never give 1 star, but you get the idea. But damn, she writes a good book. I just have to remind myself that "5 stars" doesn't necessarily have to equal "happy". I also have to remind myself that just because a character occassionally might act like a bitch, a crybaby, a scaredy cat, or an idiot, it doesn't mean she's not a good character. It just means she's real. I act like all those things at one time or another, and I'm a pretty good character--if I do say so myself.<br /><br />I liked this one more than I liked the first in the trilogy, and I want the third book <i>right now</i>, not a year from now. Ugh.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_166281066" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166281066" />
    <a title="Stacey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1020736-stacey"><img alt="Stacey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391972803p2/1020736.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166281066?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey" href="/user/show/1020736-stacey">Stacey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780375895425" href="/book/show/7825640-the-dead-tossed-waves">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1020736-stacey?shelf=my-review-or-notes">my-review-or-notes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1020736-stacey?shelf=children-and-young-adult">children-and-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1020736-stacey?shelf=borrowed-from-library">borrowed-from-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1020736-stacey?shelf=books-by-women">books-by-women</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166281066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13543592916517440693">If anything, <i>The Dead-Tossed Waves</i> is as much about what it is to be a teenaged girl, as it is about the walking dead. Sure, there's no shortage of creepy corpses, and we know everything has gone to hell-on-earth, and the zombies are winning. But it isn't the <i>mudo</i> that kept me up past one o'clock in the morning finishing the story, it was Gabry's emotion. Reading this, not only could I remember what it was like to be 16 and in love, I could almost feel it. Remember that? When nothing else could </span>
  <span id="freeText13543592916517440693" style="display:none">If anything, <i>The Dead-Tossed Waves</i> is as much about what it is to be a teenaged girl, as it is about the walking dead. Sure, there's no shortage of creepy corpses, and we know everything has gone to hell-on-earth, and the zombies are winning. But it isn't the <i>mudo</i> that kept me up past one o'clock in the morning finishing the story, it was Gabry's emotion. Reading this, not only could I remember what it was like to be 16 and in love, I could almost feel it. Remember that? When nothing else could ever be so important as being madly in love with a boy, and replaying that moment over and over when you sat so close, and almost kissed? I'm glad those days are over, and glad I'll never go back, but wow do I ever remember! <br /><br /><i>The Dead-Tossed Waves</i> is as much young adult romance novel as horror. As a zombie novel, the setting is unique because it's generations past the apocalyptic crisis. It's POST post - so far past that the youngest generations (many of them) don't even believe the “legends” of airplanes, cities, and science. These parts of the story are interesting, but the real “action” is the angst and excitement of teenaged love. A glance or brush of the hand can be as devastating or life-affirming as an encounter with the undead. <br /><br />With 16 well before the half-way point in my life, I can't help but read the story with an almost jaded eye of the adult telling the child “oh honey, there are bigger things than kissing that boy.” But then I remember the boy I never kissed, and the boy I did, and I know that was the most important thing in all of my existence in that moment, and the house could have fallen down around me without my notice. <br /><br />Ryan makes an interesting choice for a series; instead of following a single storyline through books #1 and #2, she chooses a different character, separating her stories by many years. All indications are that the third book is the same. This is a bit disconcerting, since both <i>The Forest of Hands and Teeth</i>, and <i>The Dead-Tossed Waves</i> end with cliffhangers. <i>The Forest's</i> cliffhanger is obliquely resolved with a few references in <i>Dead-Tossed</i>. I'm going to guess that <i>The Dark and Hollow Places</i> (Book #3,) will do something similar with <i>Dead-Tossed</i>'s ending. <br /><br />All of that being said, in general, I prefer my characters to have a bit more self-awareness than the main character, Gabry. These books are not heavy on character development, and although they are written in a style that suggests it's all about the individuals, everyone in this story is a character sketch. Very few of them have more than roughly drawn backstories or motivations. And even Gabry's teenaged disquiets and euphorias really exclude all other development of her character. In fact, there are more things in these stories that should have caused me to hate them, than there are to compel me to read them – and yet, 1am passed me by without blinking. <br /><br />I suppose the biggest redeeming quality, for me, is that I love the way Ryan writes. I love the cadence of her words, her descriptions, her pacing... I suspect that I could read a story about the itsy-bitsy spider climbing his spout, and if it were written by her, I'd get sucked in, even if it went on for 100 pages. <br /><br />3 stars because, as a story, it's a only a wee bit more than okay, but an extra star for making me embrace the okay-ness. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13543592916517440693" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_156582059" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156582059" />
    <a title="Sesana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana"><img alt="Sesana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413088169p2/5172893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156582059?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=monsters">monsters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156582059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9036469123017644816">Sadly, this book left me feeling pretty cross towards Carrie Ryan. I wanted to love this book with every page, but in the end, I can't. And yet it came so close to being amazing.<br/><br/>I think that Ryan is a talented writer. Her world-building is vivid and believable, though it does build on the work of others. She can craft stunningly creepy scenarios. (Imagine traveling through the Forest at night. You can hear the zombies all around you, but you can't see them. The only thing keeping them from eatin</span>
  <span id="freeText9036469123017644816" style="display:none">Sadly, this book left me feeling pretty cross towards Carrie Ryan. I wanted to love this book with every page, but in the end, I can't. And yet it came so close to being amazing.<br /><br />I think that Ryan is a talented writer. Her world-building is vivid and believable, though it does build on the work of others. She can craft stunningly creepy scenarios. (Imagine traveling through the Forest at night. You can hear the zombies all around you, but you can't see them. The only thing keeping them from eating or turning you is a rusty chainlink fence. True nightmare material.) She raises some interesting and probably unanswerable questions about the nature of unlife as a zombie. Is anything left? Or is the person you were just gone? <br /><br />Sadly, the main character is much more concerned about which boy she'll kiss next to worry too much about life after undeath. I didn't really like Mary, because I thought that she was selfish (though I did eventually mostly understand her need to see the ocean. what was left for her but that dream by then?) but I'd take her over Gabrielle any day. Gabry was a far weaker main character, and way too focused on her bland and unconvincing love triangle. I don't have the first idea why Elias would be interested in her at all <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[though there are some creepy undertones when you find out that she's the twin of the girl he calls his sister <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and even if he were, he was so much less appealing than Catcher that I couldn't understand why Gabry was that interested in him. The resolution is a foregone conclusion immediately. And honestly, the whole thing wasn't needed. Please, stop the unconvincing love triangles!<br /><br />With a more interesting love triangle, or even just a single romantic interest, or even (gasp!) no love interest at all, I would have enjoyed the book a lot more. Please, more zombies, less angsting. But what the book really needed was a stronger heroine, and Gabry was just not it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9036469123017644816" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_135721910" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135721910" />
    <a title="Ceilidh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3229028-ceilidh"><img alt="Ceilidh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422140120p2/3229028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135721910?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ceilidh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ceilidh" href="/user/show/3229028-ceilidh">Ceilidh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135721910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3945105164213041625">‘The Dead Tossed Waves’ seriously surprised me. While I still had similar problems that I had with the first book, Ryan’s wonderful prose kept me gripped throughout. She has a serious gift for creating fear out of the small moments and that which we find to be so normal, like the ocean (water zombies FTW!) The feeling of claustrophobia, even in the wide open spaces that Gabry lives in, is constant, and Ryan does a fantastic job of crafting a secret filled, constraining society in a situation whe</span>
  <span id="freeText3945105164213041625" style="display:none">‘The Dead Tossed Waves’ seriously surprised me. While I still had similar problems that I had with the first book, Ryan’s wonderful prose kept me gripped throughout. She has a serious gift for creating fear out of the small moments and that which we find to be so normal, like the ocean (water zombies FTW!) The feeling of claustrophobia, even in the wide open spaces that Gabry lives in, is constant, and Ryan does a fantastic job of crafting a secret filled, constraining society in a situation where one would think such a thing isn’t even possible. We also get answers to questions posed in the first book which is always a good thing. The mythos of the zombies, known here as the Mudo, is fleshed out further, no pun intended, and we get a wider view of how the world has been affected by the epidemic. There are some very interesting twists in this tale that I won’t spoil for you. <br /><br />But the love triangle problem looms in the distance and I just can’t ignore it. I was seriously bugged by Mary’s love-sick moping in ‘The Forest of Hands and Teeth’ because it seemed like a ridiculous priority to have when one’s life is at stake and it just dragged the plot down and sadly the exact thing happens here. While I like the protagonist in this book more than I did with Mary, it still feels highly unnecessary and uninteresting. Like her mother, Gabry suffers from some real moments of head-desk inducing stupidity. The adult Mary also gets a couple moments to display her unchanging personality from the first book. I’m disappointed that Ryan decided to repeat this plot element from the first book since it was evidently the weakest part of the story and weighed down the rest of it so much. I’d love to see her try this story without the love element in it. She manages to pose some very intriguing philosophical questions – what does it truly mean to be alive? When you are undead are you still you? – in an interesting way that keeps the plot moving, as well as some genuinely eerie moments, mixing together themes of religion, power and responsibility, and they’re all so much more interesting than the teenage romance, although I give credit to Gabry for being so much less selfish than her mother, even if she does spend a lot of time comparing herself to her. I’d love to see a story set in this world around the time of the Return. It would probably be as depressing as hell but Ryan could definitely pull it off. <br /><br />I will definitely be picking up the final book in Ryan’s trilogy, ‘The Dark and Hollow Places.’ Soap opera moments and unnecessary love triangle aside, I love Ryan’s prose and the world she has created. ‘The Dead Tossed Waves’ builds upon its predecessor and even beats it on several levels and I was highly satisfied with it. Ryan’s a great storyteller and I hope she sticks with the stuff she’s great at and makes the final book in her trilogy everything it deserves to be. <br /><br />3.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3945105164213041625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_107664255" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107664255" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107664255?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to ~Tina~ by: </span>
      Morgan's review made me.
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=lib">lib</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=apocalyptic-dystopian">apocalyptic-dystopian</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107664255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1750558717183957669">4.5 Stars<br/><br/>In all honestly, I had no intentions what so ever for reading this book. I didn't really care for the first one, <i> The Forest of Hands and Teeth</i>, and while I think the writing was fantastic, I found the tone of that book to be absolutely miserable, depressing and painful.<br/>So, when I found this at my library, I got curious and looked up reviews and realized that this isn't Mary's story, and that it was about her daughter, Gabry. That got me mighty curious and I'm so glad I took this chance</span>
  <span id="freeText1750558717183957669" style="display:none">4.5 Stars<br /><br />In all honestly, I had no intentions what so ever for reading this book. I didn't really care for the first one, <i> The Forest of Hands and Teeth</i>, and while I think the writing was fantastic, I found the tone of that book to be absolutely miserable, depressing and painful.<br />So, when I found this at my library, I got curious and looked up reviews and realized that this isn't Mary's story, and that it was about her daughter, Gabry. That got me mighty curious and I'm so glad I took this chance, cause <br /><b>The Dead-Tossed Waves</b> is an excellent read!<br /><br />Very rarely do I see sequels or companions in this case, better then the first, so I'm actually very shocked at how much I enjoyed this book. Seriously, this was much, much better! The writing flows beautiful and has such an intense mix of sadness and hope to the plot that it's hard to stop reading, so I devoured this in one sitting.<br /> <br />It's fast paced and the plot thickens up as we meet new characters, find there roles and hear there stories. <br />I loved to hate Daniel, I was just as tossed up between Catcher and Elias as Gabry was, and I even found Mary redeemable from the first one.<br />This book still lines with a lot of misery and pain, which is my reason for a lack of half a star, but it had sweet touches of romance that was seriously lacking in the first one.<br />All in all I'm thrilled that I gave this a chance, I found this experience shockingly much more pleasant then I thought I would.<br /><br />Action packed, highly entertaining and creepy enough to get right under your skin!<br />For anyone who didn't like the first should give this one a definitely go! I'm looking forward to reading the next installment into this world.<br /><br />A Must Read!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1750558717183957669" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_110814024" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/110814024" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/110814024?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer110814024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5760826639790721423">This book revolves around Gabry, the daughter of Mary, who was the protagonist in <i>The Forest of Hands and Teeth</i>. Unlike Mary, Gabry has always known safety inside the lighthouse shes grown up in. That's why one night outside the barriers - the only protection from the terrifying Mudo - comes with startling consequences that will forever alter Gabry's life.<br/><br/>One thing that really stood out to me about this book was the difference between Gabry and Mary. I liked how the author made it easy to tell t</span>
  <span id="freeText5760826639790721423" style="display:none">This book revolves around Gabry, the daughter of Mary, who was the protagonist in <i>The Forest of Hands and Teeth</i>. Unlike Mary, Gabry has always known safety inside the lighthouse shes grown up in. That's why one night outside the barriers - the only protection from the terrifying Mudo - comes with startling consequences that will forever alter Gabry's life.<br /><br />One thing that really stood out to me about this book was the difference between Gabry and Mary. I liked how the author made it easy to tell the two apart, instead of using a consistent tone in both novels (which would have been misleading). Although Gabry was ultimately easier to sympathize with, she often reflected on the past to the point where there were paragraphs devoted to the "what if I did this instead" and the "what I should have done". The writing in this one was stronger than <i>The Forest of Hands and Teeth</i> but not perfect.<br /><br />Once again, the Mudo, aka Unconsecrated, were horrifying and revolting. In <i>The Dead-Tossed Waves</i> the characters seemed to think more about the actual transformation - they pondered whether or not an individual should still be considered living, or dead, or somewhere in between. That provided the plot with a little something extra on top of the fear fest and love triangle.<br /><br />While hope was not the most prevalent theme in Carrie Ryan's second novel, I am still looking forward to seeing where she takes the story from here.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5760826639790721423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3268036659220413463">Warning....   <span id="freeText3268036659220413463" style="display:none">Warning.... Spoilers and Cursing<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Man, this book pissed me off. The first book, was a complex story of a girl who did not understand the world around her, and as she struggled to find her place in the world, frakking zombies appeared everywhere. It was awesome!<br />This second story follows Gabry, the daughter of the Mary from the first book, and her struggles to find herself and love, and zombies of course. However, there was a similar love triangle, and Gabry herself, is completely annoying. I get that she is going through some serious teen angst, but every time she comes to a sense of understand, something happens and she is right back where she started. And how can she struggle to kill a mudo, but have relatively no guilt/concern about killing a real person? The author also repeats a lot of narrative devices which seems sophomoric. <br />The story line is solid, tracing your roots back to understand your self. There are new groups introduced who have questionable intentions (The Recruiters, The Soullers); and there is also a philosophical discussion of what is life about, how if life is living, do the mudo have any kind of life or real purpose? <br />But I was really routing for the zombies to finish the girl off from the first chapter.</span>

<div id="review_52302687" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/52302687" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496094866p2/1310688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/52302687?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=signed-books">signed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52302687" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10423494492036024525">The Dead-Tossed Waves isn't really a sequel to The Forest of Hands of Teeth but more of a companion novel. Still has some of the same characters as The Forest of Hands and Teeth, still set in the same world, but it's a few years later and it follows Gabry, the daughter of Mary who was the main character in The Forest of Hands and Teeth.<br/><br/>As with it's predecessor the writing in The Dead-Tossed Waves is exemplary. Ryan's talent emanates from the pages, amidst her descriptions of the world she's crea</span>
  <span id="freeText10423494492036024525" style="display:none">The Dead-Tossed Waves isn't really a sequel to The Forest of Hands of Teeth but more of a companion novel. Still has some of the same characters as The Forest of Hands and Teeth, still set in the same world, but it's a few years later and it follows Gabry, the daughter of Mary who was the main character in The Forest of Hands and Teeth.<br /><br />As with it's predecessor the writing in The Dead-Tossed Waves is exemplary. Ryan's talent emanates from the pages, amidst her descriptions of the world she's created, in relaying the desperation of her characters, it's immensely powerful as a reader.<br /><br />It was captivating and suspenseful. Yet, at the same time it was very depressing. I often feel the glimpse of an underlying current of hope, but it seemed diminish at every opportunity. This book put me in a very solemn mood. I just wanted something for once to go right. The whole situation itself is very depressing, Gabry's situation, the world she lives in, the lives lost.... and I so wanted something hopeful.<br /><br />I loved how Ryan masterfully connected the two novels, how all the characters were somehow connected. I definitely never saw it coming.<br /><br />Overall this was a spectacular novel, I can't wait to see where the story takes us next.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10423494492036024525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1540197909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12873134857002999820">Eh. I'm kinda over this series. <br/><br/>It's been a couple of decades since Mary reached the ocean with the lighthouse, and this time the story is centered around her daughter: Gabrielle. <br/><br/>In terms of plot, stuff happens but it's very similar to what we read in the first book. There's love, an evil organization bent on hammering some sense into the protag and her friends, an escape and lotsa hungry zombies. I feel like the addition of Modu-worshipping Soulers had a lot of potential but it's a shame that </span>
  <span id="freeText12873134857002999820" style="display:none">Eh. I'm kinda over this series. <br /><br />It's been a couple of decades since Mary reached the ocean with the lighthouse, and this time the story is centered around her daughter: Gabrielle. <br /><br />In terms of plot, stuff happens but it's very similar to what we read in the first book. There's love, an evil organization bent on hammering some sense into the protag and her friends, an escape and lotsa hungry zombies. I feel like the addition of Modu-worshipping Soulers had a lot of potential but it's a shame that they only had minimal presence. <br /><br />In terms of writing, the emotions are still intense, and repeatedly listed off. The protag is still borderline useless and hysterical. It's still a little tough to get through all the angst and drama, but unlike the previous book, the pay off isn't there. They don't even reach their destination which was a disappointment.<br /><br />Gabrielle an her story is just not as fun as Mary's. And unfortunately, I don't think I'll be completing the series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12873134857002999820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Iicz9HLJcnfGOD8vvBGvkiW2xFMTS3QrZ7t1nHH+s3HBoDBniyBcYfRn1htCGl2+n5vto18D7Lf+2dM5hZi+7g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zcJotJCMkT/qKEuFSSpBLYhl2do+kYGvHs6E2XAWroYuRWsnaWW/Kdh3orG3IbMBMkjwKnLZGTOHrCJ8hHCjGQ==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText9847880428495777300" style="display:none">Carrie Ryan is the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of a lot of books. She use to be a lawyer. Happily, she is not anymore. You can keep it that way by reading her books:<br /><br />If you like zombies, try the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3432478._Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth" title=" Forest of Hands and Teeth" rel="nofollow noopener"> Forest of Hands and Teeth</a> series.<br /><br />If you like clever, fun adventure fantasy for 8-12 year olds, definitely read the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20980662._Map_To_Everywhere" title=" Map To Everywhere" rel="nofollow noopener"> Map To Everywhere</a> series (co-written with her husband, John Parke Davis).<br /><br />If you like cold calculated revenge involving hidden identities and lots of secrets: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23281652._Daughter_of_Deep_Silence" title=" Daughter of Deep Silence" rel="nofollow noopener"> Daughter of Deep Silence</a>.<br /><br />If you or your kids like multi-author, multi-platform series like 39 Clues and Spirit Animals, try <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13356177._Infinity_Ring__Divide_and_Conquer" title=" Infinity Ring: Divide and Conquer" rel="nofollow noopener"> Infinity Ring: Divide and Conquer</a> -- it's produced by the same publisher (and has vikings and true history!)<br /><br />If you like true-crime stuff (both fiction and podcasts), <b>check out her upcoming release, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40490159._Dead_Air" title=" Dead Air" rel="nofollow noopener"> Dead Air</a>, a serialized thriller co-written with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1951011._Gwenda_Bond" title=" Gwenda Bond" rel="nofollow noopener"> Gwenda Bond</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15292._Rachel_Caine" title=" Rachel Caine" rel="nofollow noopener"> Rachel Caine</a>.</b><br /><br />If you're pretty sure you won't survive the zombie apocalypse, you're in good company. When the fence is breached and her world is thrown into chaos, she must choose between her village and her future—between the one she loves and the one who loves her.
